class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola Mobility</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medion" title="Medion">Medion</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.lenovo.com.cn/">www<wbr />.lenovo<wbr />.com<wbr />.cn</a></span> <span class="mw-valign-text-top noprint" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q14799#P856" title="Edit this at Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this at Wikidata" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/10px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" decoding="async" width="10" height="10" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/15px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Lenovo Group Limited</b>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">trading as</a> <b>Lenovo</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">lə-<span style="font-size:90%">NOH</span>-voh</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh">联想</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>&#58; <i><span lang="zh-Latn">Liánxiǎng</span></i>), is a Chinese<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology company</a> specializing in designing, manufacturing, and marketing <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computers</a>, software, business solutions, and related services.<sup id="cite_ref-Locations_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locations-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Products manufactured by the company include <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">laptops</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_smartphones" title="Lenovo smartphones">smartphones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workstation" title="Workstation">workstations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Server_(computing)" title="Server (computing)">servers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">supercomputers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_storage" title="Data storage">data storage</a> devices, IT management software, and <a href="/wiki/Smart_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Smart television">smart televisions</a>. Its best-known brands include its <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</a> business line of laptop computers (acquired from <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>), the <a href="/wiki/IdeaPad" title="IdeaPad">IdeaPad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_Yoga" title="Lenovo Yoga">Yoga</a>, LOQ, and <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_Legion" title="Lenovo Legion">Legion</a> consumer lines of laptop computers, and the <a href="/wiki/IdeaCentre" title="IdeaCentre">IdeaCentre</a>, LOQ, Legion, and <a href="/wiki/ThinkCentre" title="ThinkCentre">ThinkCentre</a> lines of desktop computers. As of 2024,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo is the <a href="/wiki/Market_share_of_personal_computer_vendors" title="Market share of personal computer vendors">world's largest personal computer vendor</a> by unit sales.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo has operations in over 60 countries,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and sells its products in around 180 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It was incorporated in Hong Kong,<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> with global headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morrisville,_North_Carolina" title="Morrisville, North Carolina">Morrisville, North Carolina</a>, United States.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It has research centres in Beijing, <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yamato,_Kanagawa" title="Yamato, Kanagawa">Yamato</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kanagawa_Prefecture" title="Kanagawa Prefecture">Kanagawa Prefecture</a>, Japan), Singapore, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a>, and Morrisville,<sup id="cite_ref-Locations_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locations-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and also has Lenovo NEC Holdings, a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/NEC" title="NEC">NEC</a> that produces personal computers for the Japanese market.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1984.E2.80.931993:_Founding_and_early_history"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1984–1993:_Founding_and_early_history">1984–1993: Founding and early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1984–1993: Founding and early history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3><p>
Lenovo was founded in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> on 1 November 1984 as <b>Legend</b> by a team of engineers led by <a href="/wiki/Liu_Chuanzhi" title="Liu Chuanzhi">Liu Chuanzhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Lui" title="Danny Lui">Danny Lui</a>. Initially specializing in <a href="/wiki/Televisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Televisions">televisions</a>, the company migrated towards manufacturing and marketing computers.</p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg/220px-BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg/330px-BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg/440px-BeijingInstituteOfComputingTechnologyChineseAcademyOfSciences.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>In 1984, Lenovo was founded in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> by a team of 4 guards in a shack from the Institute of Computing Technology of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Chinese Academy of Sciences">Chinese Academy of Sciences</a> (CAS), led by <a href="/wiki/Liu_Chuanzhi" title="Liu Chuanzhi">Liu Chuanzhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Liu_Chuanzhi" title="Liu Chuanzhi">Liu Chuanzhi</a> and his group of ten experienced <a href="/wiki/Engineer" title="Engineer">engineers</a>, teaming up with <a href="/wiki/Danny_Lui" title="Danny Lui">Danny Lui</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> officially founded Lenovo in Beijing on November 1, 1984, with 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">yuan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NikeiaAsia_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NikeiaAsia-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The Chinese government approved Lenovo's incorporation on the same day. Jia Xufu (贾续福), one of the founders of Lenovo, indicated that the first meeting in preparation for starting the company was held on October 17 the same year. Eleven people, the entirety of the initial staff, attended. Each of the founders was a member of the Institute of Computing Technology of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Chinese Academy of Sciences">Chinese Academy of Sciences</a> (CAS). The 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Yuan_(currency)" title="Yuan (currency)">yuan</a> used as start-up capital was approved by Zeng Maochao (曾茂朝). The name for the company agreed upon at this meeting was the Chinese Academy of Sciences Computer Technology Research Institute New Technology Development Company.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo has increasingly diversified from the personal computer market and made a number of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_acquisition" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporate acquisition">corporate acquisitions</a>, with the most notable being acquiring and integrating most of <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s personal computer business and its x86-based server business as well as creating its own <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The organizational structure of the company was established in 1985 after the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a>. It included technology, engineering, administrative, and office departments.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The group first attempted to import televisions but failed. It rebuilt itself as a company doing quality checks on computers. It also tried and failed to market a digital watch.<sup id="cite_ref-chief_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chief-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yang_yuanqing_lenovo_ceo_by_bill_cramer.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Yang_yuanqing_lenovo_ceo_by_bill_cramer.jpg/220px-Yang_yuanqing_lenovo_ceo_by_bill_cramer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="308" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Yang_yuanqing_lenovo_ceo_by_bill_cramer.jpg/330px-Yang_yuanqing_lenovo_ceo_by_bill_cramer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Yang_yuanqing_lenovo_ceo_by_bill_cramer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="429" data-file-height="600" /></a><figcaption>Yang Yuanqing in 2008</figcaption></figure>
<p>In May 1988, Lenovo placed its first recruitment advertisement on the front page of the <i>China Youth News</i>. Such ads were quite rare in China at the time. Out of the 500 respondents, 280 were selected to take a written employment exam. 120 of these candidates were interviewed in person. Although interviewers initially only had the authority to hire 16 people, 58 were given offers. The new staff included 18 people with graduate degrees, 37 with undergraduate degrees, and three students with no university-level education. <a href="/wiki/Yang_Yuanqing" title="Yang Yuanqing">Yang Yuanqing</a>, the current chairman and CEO of Lenovo, was among that group.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Liu Chuanzhi received government permission to form a subsidiary in Hong Kong and to move there along with five other employees. Liu's father, already in Hong Kong along with Lui, furthered his son's ambitions through mentoring and facilitating loans. Liu moved to Hong Kong in 1988. To save money during this period, Liu and his co-workers walked instead of taking public transportation. To keep up appearances, they rented hotel rooms for meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1990, Lenovo started to manufacture and market computers using its own brand name.<sup id="cite_ref-chief_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chief-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Some of the company's early successes included the KT8920 mainframe computer.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It also developed a circuit board that allowed IBM-compatible personal computers to process Chinese characters.<sup id="cite_ref-chief_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chief-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1994.E2.80.931998:_IPO.2C_second_offerings_and_bond_sales"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994–1998:_IPO,_second_offerings_and_bond_sales">1994–1998: IPO, second offerings and bond sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1994–1998: IPO, second offerings and bond sales"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo (known at the time as Legend) became publicly traded after a 1994 Hong Kong <a href="/wiki/IPO" class="mw-redirect" title="IPO">IPO</a> that raised nearly <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>30 million</span><sup id="cite_ref-MITbook_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITbook-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> at <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_dollar" title="Hong Kong dollar">HK$</a>1.33</span> per share.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the IPO, many analysts were optimistic about Lenovo. On its first day of trading, the company's stock price hit a high of <span style="white-space: nowrap">HK$2.07</span> and closed at <span style="white-space: nowrap">HK$2.00</span> suggesting an initial under-valuing of the company. Proceeds from the offering were used to finance sales offices in Europe, North America and Australia, to expand and improve production and research and development, and to increase working capital.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1996, Lenovo was the market leader in China and began selling its own laptop.<sup id="cite_ref-MITbook_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITbook-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> By 1998 it held 43 per cent of the domestic computer market share in China, selling approximately one million computers.<sup id="cite_ref-MITbook_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITbook-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo released its Tianxi (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">天禧</span></span>) computer in 1998. Designed to make it easy for inexperienced Chinese consumers to use computers and access the internet, one of its most important features was a button that instantly connected users to the internet and opened the Web browser. It was co-branded with <a href="/wiki/China_Telecom" title="China Telecom">China Telecom</a> and it was bundled with one year of Internet service. The Tianxi was released in 1998. It was the result of two years of research and development. It had a pastel-colored, shell-shaped case and a seven-port USB hub under its screen. As of 2000, the Tianxi was the best-selling computer in Chinese history. It sold more than 1,000,000 units in 2000 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-Tianxi_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tianxi-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932010:_IBM_purchase_and_sale_of_smartphone_division"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999–2010:_IBM_purchase_and_sale_of_smartphone_division">1999–2010: IBM purchase and sale of smartphone division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1999–2010: IBM purchase and sale of smartphone division"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg/220px-Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg/330px-Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg/440px-Lenovo_ThinkPad_Logo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>The ThinkPad logo, as seen on the <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_ThinkPad_X100e" title="Lenovo ThinkPad X100e">Lenovo ThinkPad X100e</a> laptop computer. Lenovo purchased the ThinkPad line from <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> in 2005.</figcaption></figure><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_the_IBM_PC_business_by_Lenovo" title="Acquisition of the IBM PC business by Lenovo">Acquisition of the IBM PC business by Lenovo</a></div>
<p>To fund its continued growth, Lenovo issued a secondary offering of 50 million shares on the Hong Kong market in March 2000 and raised about <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>212 million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It rebranded to the name Lenovo in 2003 and began making acquisitions to expand the company.<sup id="cite_ref-MITbook_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MITbook-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo acquired <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s personal computer business in 2005, including the <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</a> laptop and <a href="/wiki/ThinkCentre" title="ThinkCentre">ThinkCentre</a> desktop lines.<sup id="cite_ref-sumner2005_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sumner2005-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo's acquisition of IBM's personal computer division accelerated access to foreign markets while improving Lenovo's branding and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-MW1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MW1-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo paid <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.25 billion</span> for IBM's computer business and assumed an additional <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500 million</span> of IBM's debt. This acquisition made Lenovo the third-largest computer maker worldwide by volume.<sup id="cite_ref-People_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo's purchase of the Think line from IBM also led to the creation of the IBM/Lenovo partnership, which works together in the creation of Think-line of products sold by Lenovo.
</p><p>On the purchase of IBM's personal computer division, Chuanzhi said in 2012: "We benefited in three ways from the IBM acquisition. We got the ThinkPad brand, IBM's more advanced PC manufacturing technology and the company's international resources, such as its global sales channels and operation teams. These three elements have shored up our sales revenue in the past several years."<sup id="cite_ref-People_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The employees of the division, including those who developed ThinkPad laptops and Think Centre desktops, became employees of Lenovo.
</p><p>Despite Lenovo acquiring the "Think" brand from IBM, IBM still plays a key indirect, background role in the design and production of the Think line of products. Today, IBM is responsible for overseeing servicing and repair centers, and is considered an authorized distributor and refurbisher of the Think line of products produced by Lenovo.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>IBM also acquired an 18.9% share of Lenovo in 2005 as part of Lenovo's purchase of IBM's personal computing division.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In the years following the deal, IBM sold their stake in Lenovo, with a final sale in 2011 completing their divestment.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mary_Ma" title="Mary Ma">Mary Ma</a>, Lenovo's chief financial officer from 1990 to 2007, was in charge of investor relations. Under her leadership, Lenovo successfully integrated Western-style accountability into its corporate culture. Lenovo's emphasis on transparency earned it a reputation for the best corporate governance among mainland Chinese firms. While Hong Kong-listed firms were only required to issue financial reports twice per year, Lenovo followed the international norm of issuing quarterly reports. Lenovo created an audit committee and a compensation committee with non-management directors. The company started roadshows twice per year to meet institutional investors. Ma organized the first-ever investor relations conference held in mainland China. The conference was held in Beijing in 2002 and televised on <a href="/wiki/China_Central_Television" title="China Central Television">China Central Television</a> (CCTV). Liu and Ma co-hosted the conference and both gave speeches on corporate governance.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo sold its smartphone and tablet division in 2008 for <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>100 million</span> in order to focus on personal computers and then paid US$200 million to buy it back in November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-China_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the mobile division ranked third in terms of unit share in China's mobile handset market.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo invested <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">CN¥</a>100 million in a fund dedicated to providing seed funding for mobile application development for its LeGarden online <a href="/wiki/App_store" title="App store">app store</a>. As of 2010, LeGarden had more than 1,000 programs available for the LePhone. At the same time, LeGarden counted 2,774 individual developers and 542 developer companies as members.<sup id="cite_ref-LeGarden_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeGarden-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932013:_Re-entering_smartphone_market_and_other_ventures"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2013:_Re-entering_smartphone_market_and_other_ventures">2011–2013: Re-entering smartphone market and other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2011–2013: Re-entering smartphone market and other ventures"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:VibeXLaunch.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/VibeXLaunch.jpg/220px-VibeXLaunch.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/VibeXLaunch.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="228" /></a><figcaption>The Lenovo <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_Vibe_X" title="Lenovo Vibe X">Vibe X</a> smartphone at a launch event, 2014</figcaption></figure>
<p>On January 27, 2011, Lenovo formed a joint venture to produce personal computers with Japanese electronics firm <a href="/wiki/NEC" title="NEC">NEC</a>. The companies said in a statement that they would establish a new company called Lenovo NEC Holdings, to be registered in the Netherlands. NEC received US$175 million in Lenovo stock. Lenovo was to own a 51% stake in the joint venture, while NEC would have 49%. Lenovo has a five-year option to expand its stake in the joint venture.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This joint venture was intended to boost Lenovo's worldwide sales by expanding its presence in Japan, a key market for personal computers. NEC spun off its personal computer business into the joint venture. As of 2010, NEC controlled about 20% of Japan's market for personal computers while Lenovo had a 5% share. Lenovo and NEC also agreed to explore cooperating in other areas such as servers and tablet computers.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roderick Lappin, chairman of the Lenovo–NEC joint venture, told the press that the two companies will expand their co-operation to include the development of tablet computers.<sup id="cite_ref-ET_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ET-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2011, Lenovo announced that it planned to acquire control of <a href="/wiki/Medion" title="Medion">Medion</a>, a German electronics manufacturing company. Lenovo said the acquisition would double its share of the German computer market, making it the third-largest vendor by sales (after <a href="/wiki/Acer_Inc." title="Acer Inc.">Acer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>). The deal, which closed in the third quarter of the same year, was claimed by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> as "the first in which a Chinese company acquired a well-known German company."<sup id="cite_ref-Kraut_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraut-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This acquisition will give Lenovo 14% of the German computer market. Gerd Brachmann, chairman of Medion, agreed to sell two-thirds of his 60 per cent stake in the company. He will be paid in cash for 80 per cent of the shares and will receive 20 per cent in Lenovo stock. That would give him about one per cent of Lenovo.<sup id="cite_ref-Kraut_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraut-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2012, Lenovo agreed to acquire the <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>-based electronics company Digibras, which sells products under the brand-name CCE, for a base price of 300 million <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">reales</a> (US$148 million) in a combination of stock and cash. An additional payment of 400 million reales was made dependent upon performance benchmarks.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Prior to its acquisition of CCE, Lenovo already established a $30 million factory in Brazil, but Lenovo's management had felt that they needed a local partner to maximize regional growth. Lenovo cited their desire to take advantage of increased sales due to the 2014 World Cup that would be hosted by Brazil and the 2016 Summer Olympics and CCE's reputation for quality.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Following the acquisition, Lenovo announced that its subsequent acquisitions would be concentrated in software and services.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:LenovoEMCSigning.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/LenovoEMCSigning.jpg/220px-LenovoEMCSigning.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="107" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/LenovoEMCSigning.jpg/330px-LenovoEMCSigning.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/LenovoEMCSigning.jpg/440px-LenovoEMCSigning.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3354" data-file-height="1635" /></a><figcaption>The signing ceremony for the LenovoEMC joint venture, with <a href="/wiki/Yang_Yuanqing" title="Yang Yuanqing">Yang Yuanqing</a> standing in the middle (fifth from the left) in the back row</figcaption></figure>
<p>In September 2012, Lenovo agreed to acquire the United States-based software company Stoneware, in its first software acquisition. The transaction was expected to close by the end of 2012; no financial details have been disclosed.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo said that the company was acquired in order to gain access to new technology and that Stoneware is not expected to significantly affect earnings. More specifically, Stoneware was acquired to further Lenovo's efforts to improve and expand its <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.lenovo.com/ca/en/servers-storage/solutions/cloud-computing/">cloud-computing</a> services. For the two years prior to its acquisition, Stoneware partnered with Lenovo to sell its software. During this period Stoneware's sales doubled. Stoneware was founded in 2000. As of September 2012, Stoneware is based in Carmel, Indiana and has 67 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-Stoned_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stoned-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BW3_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BW3-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo re-entered the smartphone market in 2012 and quickly became the largest vendor of <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> in mainland China.<sup id="cite_ref-smartphones_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smartphones-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Entry into the smartphone market was paired with a change of strategy from "the one-size-fits-all" to a diverse portfolio of devices.<sup id="cite_ref-einhorn2013_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-einhorn2013-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> These changes were driven by the popularity of Apple's <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> and Lenovo's desire to increase its market share in mainland China. Lenovo surpassed <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> to become the No.&#160;2 provider of smartphones in the domestic Chinese market in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-einhorn2013_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-einhorn2013-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> However, with approximately 100 smartphone brands sold in China, this only equated to a 10.4% market share.<sup id="cite_ref-einhorn2013_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-einhorn2013-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, Lenovo announced an investment of US$793 million in the construction of a mobile phone manufacturing and R&amp;D facility in <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hubei" title="Hubei">Hubei</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Lenovo created a joint venture with EMC named <a href="/wiki/Iomega" title="Iomega">Iomega</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IomegaLenovoEMC.DellNews2013_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IomegaLenovoEMC.DellNews2013-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The venture took over Iomega's business and rebranded all of Iomega's products under the LenovoEMC brand, and designed products for small and medium-sized businesses that could not afford enterprise-class data storage.<sup id="cite_ref-LENOVOEMC_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LENOVOEMC-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LENOVOEMCARS_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LENOVOEMCARS-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GROUP_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GROUP-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo has since retired all of the LenovoEMC products on their product page advising that the products are no longer available for purchase on lenovo.com.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.93present:_Purchase_of_IBM_server_lines_and_other_acquisitions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–present:_Purchase_of_IBM_server_lines_and_other_acquisitions">2014–present: Purchase of IBM server lines and other acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014–present: Purchase of IBM server lines and other acquisitions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" class="thumbcaption">Corporate logo (1984–2003)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenovo_Logo.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Lenovo_Logo.svg/200px-Lenovo_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Lenovo_Logo.svg/400px-Lenovo_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="71" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Corporate logo (2003–2015)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenovo_logo_(2015_onwards)_2.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Lenovo_logo_%282015_onwards%29_2.svg/200px-Lenovo_logo_%282015_onwards%29_2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Lenovo_logo_%282015_onwards%29_2.svg/300px-Lenovo_logo_%282015_onwards%29_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Lenovo_logo_%282015_onwards%29_2.svg/400px-Lenovo_logo_%282015_onwards%29_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="6750" data-file-height="1353" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Corporate logo (2015–present)</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>IBM sold its x86-based server lines, including <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_System_x" title="Lenovo System x">System x</a> and <a href="/wiki/IBM_BladeCenter" title="IBM BladeCenter">Blade Center</a>, to Lenovo in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo says it will gain access to more enterprise customers, improve its profit margins, and develop a closer relationship with Intel, the maker of most server processors, through its acquisition of IBM's x86-based server business.<sup id="cite_ref-ForbesIBM_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ForbesIBM-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 1 October 2014, Lenovo closed its acquisition of IBM's server division, with the final price put at $2.1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo said this acquisition came in at a price lower than the previously announced $2.3 billion partially because of a change in the value of IBM inventories. The deal has been already approved by Europe and China. Per Forbes, the United States Department of Treasury <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Foreign_Investment_in_the_United_States" title="Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States">Committee on Foreign Investment in the United States</a> (CFIUS) was reportedly the last major hurdle for Lenovo, since the United States has the strictest policies. According to Timothy Prickett-Morgan from Enterprise Tech, the deal still awaits "approval of regulators in China, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, and Canada".<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After closing, Lenovo said that its goal was to become the world's largest maker of servers. Lenovo also announced plans to start integrating IBM's workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition added about 6,500 new employees to Lenovo. Lenovo said that it has no immediate intent to cut jobs. Lenovo said that positions in research and development and customer-facing roles such as marketing would be "100% protected", but expected "rationalization" of its supply chain and procurement.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Moto_X_(11236439494).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Moto_X_%2811236439494%29.jpg/170px-Moto_X_%2811236439494%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="178" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Moto_X_%2811236439494%29.jpg/255px-Moto_X_%2811236439494%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Moto_X_%2811236439494%29.jpg/340px-Moto_X_%2811236439494%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3192" data-file-height="3345" /></a><figcaption>Motorola Moto X</figcaption></figure>
<p>On 29 January 2014, Google announced it would sell <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola Mobility</a> to Lenovo for US$2.91 billion. As of February 2014, Google owned about 5.94% of Lenovo's stock. The deal included smartphone lines like the <a href="/wiki/Moto_X_(1st_generation)" title="Moto X (1st generation)">Moto X</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moto_G_(1st_generation)" title="Moto G (1st generation)">Moto G</a>, <a href="/wiki/Droid_Turbo" title="Droid Turbo">Droid Turbo</a>, and the future Motorola Mobility product roadmap, while Google retained the Advanced Technologies &amp; Projects unit and all but 2,000 of the company's patents.<sup id="cite_ref-CIO_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIO-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo received royalty free licenses to all the patents retained by Google.<sup id="cite_ref-Moneyball_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moneyball-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo received approval from the European Union for its acquisition of Motorola in June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-EU1_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU1-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition was completed on 30 October 2014. Motorola Mobility remained headquartered in Chicago, and continued to use the Motorola brand, but Liu Jun, president of Lenovo's mobile device business, became the head of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-FinalMotoDeal_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FinalMotoDeal-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj-lenovoclosed_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-lenovoclosed-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2014, Lenovo purchased a portfolio of patents from <a href="/wiki/NEC" title="NEC">NEC</a> related to mobile technology. These included over 3,800 patent families in countries around the world. The purchase included standards-essential patents for 3G and LTE cellular technologies and other patents related to smartphones and tablets.<sup id="cite_ref-PAT1_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAT1-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2015, Lenovo revealed a new logo at Lenovo Tech World in Beijing, with the slogan "Innovation Never Stands Still" (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh">创新无止境</span>). Lenovo's new logo, created by Saatchi, can be changed by its advertising agencies and sales partners, within restrictions, to fit the context. It has a lounging "e" and is surrounded by a box that can be changed to use a relevant scene, solid color, or photograph. Lenovo's Chief Marketing Officer David Roman said, "When we first started looking at it, it wasn't about just a change in typography or the look of the logo. We asked 'If we really are a net-driven, customer-centric company, what should the logo look like?' We came up with the idea of a digital logo first [...] designed to be used on the internet and adaptable to context."<sup id="cite_ref-AALogo_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AALogo-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early June 2015, Lenovo announced plans to sell up to US$650 million in five-year bonds denominated in Chinese yuan. The bonds were sold in Hong Kong with coupon ranging from 4.95% to 5.05%. This is only the second sale of bonds in Lenovo's history. Financial commentators noted that Lenovo was paying a premium to list the bonds in yuan given relatively low costs for borrowing in US dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-Bonds1_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonds1-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo said that its x86 servers will be available to all its channel partners. Lenovo plans to cut prices on x86 products in order to gain market share.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> This goes in alliance with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s vision of the future around cloud technologies and their own POWER processor architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo's acquisition of IBM's businesses is arguably one of the greatest case studies on merging massive international enterprises. Though this acquisition in 2005 ultimately resulted in success, the integration of the businesses had a difficult and challenging beginning. Lenovo had employees from different cultures, different backgrounds, and different languages.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> These differences caused misunderstandings, hampering trust and the ability to build a new corporate culture. At the end of its first two years, Lenovo Group had met many of its original challenges, including integrating two disparate cultures in the newly formed company, maintaining the Think brand image for quality and innovation, and improving supply chain and manufacturing efficiencies.<sup id="cite_ref-ibm-pcd-deal_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibm-pcd-deal-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> However, Lenovo had failed to meet a key objective of the merger: leveraging the combined strength of the two companies to grow volume and market share.<sup id="cite_ref-ibm-pcd-deal_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibm-pcd-deal-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In order to achieve success, Lenovo embraced diversification at multiple levels-  business model, culture, and talent. By 2015, Lenovo grew into the world's number 1 PC maker, number 3 smartphone manufacturer and number 3 in the production of tablet computers.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2017, Lenovo announced it was partnering with Fort Lauderdale, Florida-based software storage virtualization company <a href="/wiki/DataCore" title="DataCore">DataCore</a> to add DataCore's <a href="/wiki/Parallel_I/O" title="Parallel I/O">parallel I/O</a>-processing software to Lenovo's storage devices.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>  The servers were reportedly designed to outperform <a href="/wiki/Storage_Area_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Storage Area Network">Storage Area Network</a> (SAN) SAN arrays.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Lenovo formed a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Fujitsu" title="Fujitsu">Fujitsu</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Development_Bank_of_Japan" title="Development Bank of Japan">Development Bank of Japan</a> (DBJ).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In the joint venture, Fujitsu would sell Lenovo a 51% stake in <b>Fujitsu Client Computing Limited</b>. DBJ would acquire a 5% stake.
</p><p>In September 2018, Lenovo and <a href="/wiki/NetApp" title="NetApp">NetApp</a> announced about strategic partnership and joint venture in China. As part of strategic partnership Lenovo started two new lines of storage systems: DM-Series and DE-Series. Both storage systems using Lenovo hardware and NetApp software: DM-Series using <a href="/wiki/ONTAP" title="ONTAP">ONTAP</a> OS and DE-Series <a href="/wiki/NetApp#E-Series" title="NetApp">SANtricity</a> OS.
</p><p>In 2018, Lenovo became the world's largest provider for the <a href="/wiki/TOP500" title="TOP500">TOP500</a> <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">supercomputers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BUS_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUS-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Lenovo became a preferred data center innovation provider for <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a> starting with <a href="/wiki/Trolls_World_Tour" title="Trolls World Tour">Trolls World Tour</a>.
</p><p>On 12 January 2021, Lenovo filed an application to issue Chinese depositary receipts, representing newly issued ordinary shares, and to list them on the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Stock_Exchange_STAR_Market" title="Shanghai Stock Exchange STAR Market">Science and Technology Innovation Board</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Stock_Exchange" title="Shanghai Stock Exchange">Shanghai Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2021, Lenovo was reorganized into three divisions: The Intelligent Devices Group for PCs, Smartphones, Smart Collaboration products, Augmented and Virtual Reality solutions and Internet of Things devices, the Infrastructure Solutions Group (formally known as Data Center Group) for smart infrastructure solutions, and the Solutions and Services Group focused on services and industry-specific products.<sup id="cite_ref-Alspach_2021_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alspach_2021-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> That year, the company hit $60 billion in annual revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-Haranas_2021_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haranas_2021-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chanthadavong_2021_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chanthadavong_2021-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 October 2021, Lenovo withdrew its application to list on the Shanghai Stock Exchange just days after it had been accepted by the exchange, citing the possibility of the validity of financial information in its prospectus lapsing as the reason. The price of the company's shares on the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Stock_Exchange" title="Hong Kong Stock Exchange">Hong Kong Stock Exchange</a> dropped by over 17% following the news, which was its biggest intraday decline in over a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Name"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:CES_2012_-_Lenovo_(6764011613).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/CES_2012_-_Lenovo_%286764011613%29.jpg/220px-CES_2012_-_Lenovo_%286764011613%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/CES_2012_-_Lenovo_%286764011613%29.jpg/330px-CES_2012_-_Lenovo_%286764011613%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/CES_2012_-_Lenovo_%286764011613%29.jpg/440px-CES_2012_-_Lenovo_%286764011613%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Lenovo advertisement at the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a>, 2012</figcaption></figure>
<p>"Lenovo" is a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" class="mw-redirect" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of "Le-" (from Legend) and "novo", <a href="/wiki/Latin_ablative" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin ablative">Latin ablative</a> for "new". The Chinese name (<a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hans">联想</span>; <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">traditional Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant">聯想</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>&#58; <i><span lang="zh-Latn"><span class="ext-phonos skin-invert"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/e\/e4\/Zh-li%C3%A1nxiang.ogg\/Zh-li%C3%A1nxiang.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;label&quot;:{&quot;html&quot;:&quot;Li\u00e1nxi\u01ceng&quot;},&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;Zh-li\u00e1nxiang.ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e4/Zh-li%C3%A1nxiang.ogg/Zh-li%C3%A1nxiang.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label">Liánxiǎng</span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:Zh-li%C3%A1nxiang.ogg" title="File:Zh-liánxiang.ogg">ⓘ</a></sup></span></span></i>) means "association" (as in "association of ideas"), "associative thinking", or "connected thinking". It also implies creativity.<sup id="cite_ref-cam_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cam-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> "Lianxiang" was first used to refer to a layout of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_typewriter" title="Chinese typewriter">Chinese typewriters</a> in the 1950s organized into groups of common words and phrases rather than the standard dictionary layout.<sup id="cite_ref-Mullaney2018_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mullaney2018-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the first 20 years of its existence, the company's English name was "Legend". In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Yang_Yuanqing" title="Yang Yuanqing">Yang Yuanqing</a> decided to abandon the Legend English name to expand beyond the Chinese home market. "Legend" was already in use worldwide by many businesses,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> making it impossible to register in many jurisdictions outside China. In April 2003, the company publicly announced its new English name, "Lenovo", with an advertising campaign including huge billboards and primetime television ads. Lenovo spent 18 million <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">RMB</a> on an eight-week television advertising campaign. The billboards showed the Lenovo logo against blue sky with a slogan that read, "Transcendence depends on how you think." By the end of 2003, Lenovo had spent a total of 200 million RMB on rebranding.<sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Products and services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lenovo is a manufacturer of personal computers, smartphones, televisions, and wearable devices. Some of the company's earliest products included the KT8920 <a href="/wiki/Mainframe_computer" title="Mainframe computer">mainframe computer</a><sup id="cite_ref-book1_12-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and a circuit board that allowed IBM-compatible personal computers to process Chinese characters.<sup id="cite_ref-chief_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chief-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> One of its first computers was the Tianxi (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">天禧</span></span>), released in 1998 in the Chinese market. It became the best selling computer in Chinese history in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Tianxi_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tianxi-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_and_business_computing">Personal and business computing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Personal and business computing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo markets the <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</a>, <a href="/wiki/IdeaPad" title="IdeaPad">IdeaPad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_Yoga" title="Lenovo Yoga">Yoga</a>, Legion and Xiaoxin (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">小新</span></span>; Chinese market only) lines of laptops, as well as the <a href="/wiki/IdeaCentre" title="IdeaCentre">IdeaCentre</a> and <a href="/wiki/ThinkCentre" title="ThinkCentre">ThinkCentre</a> lines of desktops.<sup id="cite_ref-owen2011_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owen2011-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> It expanded significantly in 2005 through its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s personal computer business, including its ThinkPad and ThinkCentre lines. As of January 2013, shipments of <a href="/wiki/Think_(slogan)" title="Think (slogan)">THINK-branded</a> computers have doubled since Lenovo's takeover of the brand, with profit margins thought to be above 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-Econ1_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ1-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo aggressively expanded the THINK brand away from traditional laptop computers in favor of tablets and hybrid devices such as the <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_Tablet_2" title="ThinkPad Tablet 2">ThinkPad Tablet 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_Yoga" title="ThinkPad Yoga">ThinkPad Yoga</a>, <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_8" title="ThinkPad 8">ThinkPad 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_Helix" title="ThinkPad Helix">ThinkPad Helix</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_Twist" title="ThinkPad Twist">ThinkPad Twist</a>; the shift came as a response to the growing popularity of mobile devices, and the release of <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a> in October 2012. Lenovo achieved significant success with this high-value strategy and in 2013 controlled more than 40% of the market for Windows computers priced above $900 in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-CNET21_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNET21-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: ThinkPad"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg/220px-Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg/330px-Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg/440px-Lenovo_ThinkPad_X1_Ultrabook.jpg 2x" data-file-width="944" data-file-height="756" /></a><figcaption>The first generation <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_X1_series" title="ThinkPad X1 series">ThinkPad X1</a> Carbon from 2012 Ultrabook with extensive use of lightweight and durable carbon fibre technology<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>The ThinkPad is a line of business-oriented <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">laptop</a> known for their boxy black design, modeled after a traditional Japanese <i><a href="/wiki/Bento" title="Bento">bento</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The ThinkPad was originally an <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> product developed at the <a href="/wiki/IBM_Yamato_Facility" title="IBM Yamato Facility">Yamato Facility</a> in Japan by Arimasa Naitoh<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">内藤在正</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Naitō Arimasa</i></span>)</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> they have since been developed, manufactured and sold by both IBM and Lenovo after early 2005, following its acquisition of IBM's <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a> division. The ThinkPad has been used in space and was the only laptop model certified for use on the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> until 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ThinkCentre">ThinkCentre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: ThinkCentre"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ThinkCentre" title="ThinkCentre">ThinkCentre</a></div>
<p>The ThinkCentre is a line of business-oriented <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop computers</a> which was introduced in 2003 by IBM and since has been produced and sold by Lenovo since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_Company_History_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_Company_History-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> ThinkCentre computers typically include mid-range to high-end processors, options for discrete graphics cards, and multi-monitor support. Similar to the ThinkPad line of computers, there have been budget lines of ThinkCentre branded computers in the past. Some examples of this include: M55e series, A50 series, M72 series. These "budget" lines are typically "thin clients" however, meaning they are not standalone computers, rather, they are access points to a central server.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_-_ThinkCentre_Desktops_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_-_ThinkCentre_Desktops-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="ThinkServer.2C_followed_by_ThinkSystem"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="ThinkServer,_followed_by_ThinkSystem">ThinkServer, followed by ThinkSystem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: ThinkServer, followed by ThinkSystem"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ThinkServer" class="mw-redirect" title="ThinkServer">ThinkServer</a></div>
<p>The ThinkServer product line began with the TS100 from Lenovo.<sup id="cite_ref-PCPro_-_ThinkServer_TS100_Review_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCPro_-_ThinkServer_TS100_Review-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The server was developed under an agreement with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, by which Lenovo would produce single-socket and dual-socket servers based on IBM's xSeries technology.<sup id="cite_ref-PCPro_-_ThinkServer_TS100_Review_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCPro_-_ThinkServer_TS100_Review-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> An additional feature of the server design was a support package aimed at small businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-PCPro_-_ThinkServer_TS100_Review_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCPro_-_ThinkServer_TS100_Review-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The focus of this support package was to provide small businesses with software tools to ease the process of server management and reduce dependence on IT support.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_Blogs_-_ThinkServer_Debut_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_Blogs_-_ThinkServer_Debut-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 20, 2017, Lenovo's Data Center Group relaunched the ThinkServer product line as ThinkSystem,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> which consisted of 17 new machine type models, in the catalog formate containing form factors such as Tower, 1U/2U, Blades, Dense and 4U Mission Critical Intel-based servers.  Also within this relaunch contained a portfolio of Storage Arrays and of Fibre Channel SAN Switches and Directors.  To further incorporate industry-leading partnerships into its portfolio, Lenovo struck an agreement with the processor company, AMD, to be able to supply customers with a choice of options between both Intel and AMD powered appliances.  In August, 2019, the first two ThinkSystem platforms were introduced to the market containing a single AMD EPYC processor, the SR635 (1U) and the SR655 (2U).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>  Again, in May 2020, Lenovo DCG further expanded its AMD offerings to incorporate 2-proc systems, the SR645 and the SR665,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> continuing tio exemplify its approach to being the Most Trusted Data Center Advisor in the market.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ThinkStation">ThinkStation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: ThinkStation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ThinkStation" title="ThinkStation">ThinkStation</a></div>
<p>Lenovo ThinkStations are workstations designed for high-end computing. In 2008, IBM/Lenovo expanded the focus of its THINK brand to include workstations, with the ThinkStation S10 being the first model released.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ThinkVision">ThinkVision</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: ThinkVision"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ThinkVision" title="ThinkVision">ThinkVision</a></div>
<p>High-end monitors are marketed under the ThinkVision name. ThinkVision displays share a common design language with other THINK devices such as the <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</a> line of laptop computers and <a href="/wiki/ThinkCentre" title="ThinkCentre">ThinkCentre</a> line of desktop computers. At the 2014 International CES, Lenovo announced the ThinkVision Pro2840m, a 28-inch 4K display aimed at professionals. Lenovo also announced another 28-inch 4K touch-enabled device running Android that can function as an all-in-one PC or an external display for other devices.<sup id="cite_ref-4K_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4K-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the 2016 International CES, Lenovo announced two displays with both USB-C and DisplayPort connectivity. The ThinkVision X24 Pro monitor is a 24-inch 1920 by 1080 pixel thin-bezel display that uses an IPS LCD panel. The ThinkVision X1 is a 27-inch 3840 by 2160 pixel thin-bezel display that uses a 10-bit panel with 99% coverage of the sRGB color gamut. The X24 includes a wireless charging base for mobile phones. The X1 is the first monitor to receive the TUV Eye-Comfort certification. Both monitors have HDMI 2.0 ports, support charging laptops, mobile phones, and other devices, and have Intel RealSense 3D cameras in order to support facial recognition. Both displays have dual-array microphones and 3-watt stereo speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-Vision1_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vision1-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="IdeaPad">IdeaPad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: IdeaPad"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IdeaPad" title="IdeaPad">IdeaPad</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg/220px-Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg/330px-Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg/440px-Lenovo_IdeaPad.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a><figcaption>A Lenovo <a href="/wiki/IdeaPad_U_series" title="IdeaPad U series">IdeaPad U350</a> at a launch event in Japan, 2009</figcaption></figure>
<p>The IdeaPad line of consumer-oriented <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">laptops</a> was introduced in January 2008. The IdeaPad is the result of Lenovo's own research and development; Unlike the ThinkPad line, its design and branding were not inherited from IBM nor are they designed/developed by IBM.
</p><p>The IdeaPad's design language differs markedly from the <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPad</a> and has a more consumer-focused look and feel.<sup id="cite_ref-IdeaPad_Consumer_Oriented_Design_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IdeaPad_Consumer_Oriented_Design-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 21, 2016, Lenovo confirmed that their Yoga series is not meant to be compatible with <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">Linux</a> operating systems, that they know it is impossible to install Linux on some models, and that it is not supported.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> This came in the wake of media coverage of problems that users were having while trying to install <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu" title="Ubuntu">Ubuntu</a> on several Yoga models, including the 900 ISK2, 900 ISK For Business, 900S, and 710, which were traced back to Lenovo disabling and removing support for the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Host_Controller_Interface" title="Advanced Host Controller Interface">AHCI</a> storage mode for the device's <a href="/wiki/Solid_State_Drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Solid State Drive">Solid State Drive</a> in the computer's <a href="/wiki/BIOS" title="BIOS">BIOS</a>, in favor of a <a href="/wiki/RAID" title="RAID">RAID</a> mode that is only supported by <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a> <a href="/wiki/Device_driver" title="Device driver">drivers</a> that come with the system.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo has since released an alternative firmware that has restored the AHCI mode to the drive controller to allow installation of Linux operating systems.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="IdeaCentre">IdeaCentre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: IdeaCentre"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IdeaCentre" title="IdeaCentre">IdeaCentre</a></div>
<p>All IdeaCentres are all-in-one machines, combining processor and monitor into a single unit.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Desktops_at_CES_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Desktops_at_CES-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The desktops were described by HotHardware as being "uniquely designed".<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Desktops_at_CES_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Desktops_at_CES-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/IdeaCentre" title="IdeaCentre">IdeaCentre</a> <a href="/wiki/Desktop_computer" title="Desktop computer">desktop</a>, the IdeaCentre K210, was announced by Lenovo on 30 June 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_K210_-_TechCrunch_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_K210_-_TechCrunch-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> While the IdeaCentre line consists only of desktops, it shares design elements and features with the <a href="/wiki/IdeaPad" title="IdeaPad">IdeaPad</a> line.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_K210_-_TechCrunch_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_K210_-_TechCrunch-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> One such feature was Veriface facial recognition technology.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_K210_-_TechCrunch_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_K210_-_TechCrunch-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">CES</a> 2011, Lenovo announced the launch of four IdeaCentre desktops: the A320, B520, B320, and C205.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Desktops_at_CES_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Desktops_at_CES-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In the autumn of 2012, the firm introduced the more powerful IdeaCentre A720, with a 27-inch touchscreen display and running <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> With a TV tuner and HDMI in, the A720 can also serve as a multimedia hub or home theater PC.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_A720_Review_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo_IdeaCentre_A720_Review-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, Lenovo added a table computer to the IdeaCentre line. The <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_IdeaCentre_Horizon" title="Lenovo IdeaCentre Horizon">Lenovo IdeaCentre Horizon</a>, introduced at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a> is a 27-inch touchscreen computer designed to lay flat for simultaneous use by multiple people. Thanks to its use of Windows 8, the Horizon can also serve as a desktop computer when set upright.<sup id="cite_ref-Table_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legion_and_LOQ">Legion and LOQ</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Legion and LOQ"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_Legion" title="Lenovo Legion">Lenovo Legion</a></div>
<p>Legion is a series of laptops and tablets from Lenovo targeting gaming performance. The first Legion brand laptops was revealed at CES 2017, the Legion Y520 and the Legion Y720.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> On June 6, 2017, a high-performance model, the Legion Y920, equipped with Intel's seventh-generation quad-core i7-7820HK and Nvidia GTX 1070 discrete graphics, was launched.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At <a href="/wiki/E3_2018" title="E3 2018">E3 2018</a>, Lenovo announced three new laptops with new redesigned chassis, Y530, Y730 and Y7000.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Lenovo launched Legion 3, 5, and 7, where Legion 7 is the highest specification of the series.
</p><p>In 2021, Lenovo launched Legion 5 pro with AMD 5th series CPU and Nvidia 30s GPU.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2023, Lenovo launched the LOQ gaming sub-brand which is aimed towards budget and new-to-gaming markets.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smartphones">Smartphones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Smartphones"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_smartphones" title="Lenovo smartphones">Lenovo smartphones</a></div>
