<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg/220px-ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg/330px-ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg/440px-ThinkPad_Tablet_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4134" data-file-height="2621" /></a><figcaption>The Lenovo <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_Tablet_2" title="ThinkPad Tablet 2">ThinkPad Tablet 2</a> from front and back</figcaption></figure>
<p>As of January 2013, Lenovo only manufactured phones that use the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> operating system from <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>. Numerous press reports indicated that Lenovo planned to release a phone running <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone_8" title="Windows Phone 8">Windows Phone 8</a>, According to J.&#160;D. Howard, a vice president at Lenovo's mobile division, the company would release a Windows Phone product if there is market demand.<sup id="cite_ref-Lumia_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lumia-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo has implemented an aggressive strategy to replace <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung Electronics</a> as Mainland China market's top smartphone vendor. It has spent $793.5 million in Wuhan in order to build a plant that can produce 30 to 40 million phones per year. Data from Analysys International shows that Lenovo experienced considerable growth in smartphone sales in China during 2012. Specifically, it saw its market share increase to 14.2% during 2012's third quarter, representing an increase when compared to 4.8% in the same quarter of 2011. IDC analysts said that Lenovo's success is due to its "aggressive ramping-up and improvements in channel partnerships". Analysys International analyst Wang Ying wrote, "Lenovo possesses an obvious advantage over rivals in terms of sales channels." The company's CEO, Yang Yuanqing, said, "Lenovo does not want to be the second player ... we want to be the best. Lenovo has the confidence to outperform Samsung and Apple, at least in the Chinese market."<sup id="cite_ref-TOM_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TOM-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to IHS iSuppli, Lenovo was a top-three smartphone maker in China with a 16.5% market share in the first quarter of 2012. According to a May report released by IDC Lenovo ranks fourth in the global tablet market by volume.<sup id="cite_ref-PCMAG_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCMAG-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> As of November 2012, Lenovo was the second largest seller of mobile phones in China when measured by volume.<sup id="cite_ref-smartphones_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smartphones-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, Lenovo CEO Yang Yuanqing indicated that the company had aimed to release smartphones in the United States within the next year. Later in October, Lenovo expressed interest in acquiring the Canadian smartphone maker <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Limited" title="BlackBerry Limited">BlackBerry Limited</a>. However, its attempt was reportedly blocked by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">Government of Canada</a>, citing security concerns due to the use of BlackBerry devices by prominent members of the government. An official stated that "we have been pretty consistent that the message is Canada is open to foreign investment and investment from China in particular but not at the cost of compromising national security".<sup id="cite_ref-verge-bblenovo_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-bblenovo-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-lenovousphones_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-lenovousphones-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2014, Lenovo announced a proposed deal to acquire <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola Mobility</a> to bolster its plans for the U.S. market.<sup id="cite_ref-verge-lenovosale_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-lenovosale-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> officially announced that Lenovo had become the hardware partner of <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a> platform at the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_World_Congress" title="Mobile World Congress">Mobile World Congress</a> 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In January 2016, Lenovo announced at CES that the company would be producing the first <a href="/wiki/Tango_(platform)" title="Tango (platform)">Tango</a> phone.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo plus Motorola was the 3rd largest producer of smartphones by volume in the world between 2011 and 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-idc-2011-15_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idc-2011-15-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Since Lenovo's acquisition of Motorola Mobility, the combined global market share of Lenovo plus Motorola has fallen from 7.2% in 2014 to 3.9% in the third quarter of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-idc-smartphones-2014_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idc-smartphones-2014-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lenovo-finances-q3-2016_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lenovo-finances-q3-2016-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> A number of factors have been cited as the cause of this reduced demand, including the fact that Lenovo relied heavily on carriers to sell its phones, its phones lacked strong branding and unique features to distinguish them in the competitive Chinese market where a weak economy and saturated market is slowing demand<sup id="cite_ref-forbes-lenovo_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-lenovo-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chicagobusiness_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chicagobusiness-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and the culture clash between a more hierarchical PC company and the need to be nimble to sell rapidly-evolving smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-verge-mistakes_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-mistakes-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> In response to the weak sales, Lenovo announced in August 2015 that it would lay off 3,200 employees, mostly in its Motorola smartphone business.<sup id="cite_ref-itwire-layoffs_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itwire-layoffs-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the reorganization which followed, Lenovo was uncertain how to brand its Motorola smartphones. In November 2015, members of Lenovo management made statements that Lenovo would use the Motorola brand for all its smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-android-dissolved_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-android-dissolved-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Then, in January 2016, Lenovo announced that it would be eliminating the Motorola brand in favor of "Moto by Lenovo". The company reversed course in March 2017 and announced that the Motorola brand name would be used in all regions in future products. "In 2016, we just finished transforming ourselves," Motorola Chairman and President Aymar de Lencquesaing said in an interview, "We have clarity on how we present ourselves."<sup id="cite_ref-android-away_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-android-away-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smart_televisions">Smart televisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Smart televisions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_LeTV" title="Lenovo LeTV">Lenovo LeTV</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg/220px-Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg/330px-Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg/440px-Lenovo_A30_TV_Set_Top_Box.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="696" /></a><figcaption>A Lenovo A30 TV set-top box</figcaption></figure>
<p>In November 2011, Lenovo said it would soon unveil a <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">Smart TV</a> product called LeTV, expected for release in the first quarter of 2012. "The PC, communications and TV industries are currently undergoing a "smart" transformation. In the future, users will have many smart devices and will desire an integrated experience of hardware, software and cloud services." Liu Jun, president of Lenovo's mobile-Internet and digital-home-business division.<sup id="cite_ref-TV_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TV-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In June 2013 Lenovo announced a partnership with Sharp to produce smart televisions. In March 2014, Lenovo announced that it projected smart television sales surpassing one million units for 2014. The same month Lenovo released its flagship S9 Smart TV.<sup id="cite_ref-Smart1_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smart1-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wearables">Wearables</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Wearables"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:LenovoWatch.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/LenovoWatch.jpg/220px-LenovoWatch.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/LenovoWatch.jpg/330px-LenovoWatch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/LenovoWatch.jpg/440px-LenovoWatch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3661" data-file-height="2439" /></a><figcaption>The Lenovo Smartwatch on display at the 2015 Mobile World Congress</figcaption></figure>
<p>Rumors that Lenovo was developing a wearable device were confirmed in October 2014 after the company submitted a regulatory finding to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a>. The device, branded a "Smartband", has a battery life of seven days. It has an optical heart-rate monitor and can be used to track distance and time spent running and calories burned. It can also notify the user of incoming calls and texts.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> It can also unlock computers without the use of a password. The Smartband went on sale in October 2014. Lenovo started offering the device for sale on its website without a formal product announcement.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="IoT_.2F_Smart_Home"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="IoT_/_Smart_Home">IoT / Smart Home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: IoT / Smart Home"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2015 Lenovo launched a strategic cooperation with IngDan (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">硬蛋</span></span>), a subsidiary of Chinese electronics e-commerce company <a href="/wiki/Cogobuy_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Cogobuy Group">Cogobuy Group</a>, to penetrate into the intelligent hardware sector.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> &#160;Lenovo wanted to procure High-Tech hardware in the then newly emerging <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_Things" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet of Things">Internet of Things</a> (IoT) economy<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and formed a strategic partnership with Cogobuy in which it previously primarily bought <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC components</a> from.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>  Cogobuy's supply chain was utilised by Lenovo to procure <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer devices</a> and bridge gaps in their <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_hardware" title="Proprietary hardware">proprietary hardware</a> and software development.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>  At the IFA 2018, Lenovo launched several <a href="/wiki/Home_automation" title="Home automation">Home automation</a> products.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lenovo_Connect">Lenovo Connect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lenovo Connect"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the Mobile World Congress in 2016, Lenovo introduced Lenovo Connect, a wireless roaming service. This service works across devices, networks, and borders for customers in China and <a href="/wiki/Europe,_the_Middle_East_and_Africa" title="Europe, the Middle East and Africa">EMEA</a> (Europe, the Middle East and Africa). Lenovo Connect eliminates the need to buy new <a href="/wiki/SIM_card" title="SIM card">SIM cards</a> when crossing borders. Lenovo Connect started service for phones and select ThinkPad laptops in China in February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-LenovoConnect_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LenovoConnect-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Operations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lenovo's principal facilities are in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morrisville,_North_Carolina" title="Morrisville, North Carolina">Morrisville, North Carolina</a>, United States, with research centres in Beijing, Singapore, Morrisville, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xiamen" title="Xiamen">Xiamen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Yamato,_Kanagawa" title="Yamato, Kanagawa">Yamato</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kanagawa_Prefecture" title="Kanagawa Prefecture">Kanagawa Prefecture</a>, Japan).<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo operates manufacturing facilities in Chengdu and <a href="/wiki/Hefei" title="Hefei">Hefei</a> in China, and in Japan. A 700-square-metre (7,500&#160;sq&#160;ft) global <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> opened in Beijing in February 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-einhorn2013_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-einhorn2013-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg/220px-Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg/330px-Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg/440px-Shenzhen_Lenovo_building_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption>The Lenovo R&amp;D center in <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Lenovo's manufacturing operations are a departure from the usual industry practice of outsourcing to contract manufacturers. Lenovo instead focuses on <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertical integration</a> in order to avoid excessive reliance on <a href="/wiki/Original_equipment_manufacturer" title="Original equipment manufacturer">original equipment manufacturers</a> and to keep down costs.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Speaking on this topic, Yang Yuanqing said, "Selling PCs is like selling fresh fruit. The speed of innovation is very fast, so you must know how to keep up with the pace, control inventory, to match supply with demand and handle very fast turnover." Lenovo benefited from its vertical integration after flooding affected hard-drive manufacturers in Thailand in 2011, as the company could continue manufacturing operations by shifting production towards products for which hard drives were still available.<sup id="cite_ref-WARC_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WARC-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WS_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WS-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo began to emphasize vertical integration after a meeting in 2009 in which CEO Yang Yuanqing, and the head of Lenovo's supply chain, analyzed the costs versus the benefits of in-house manufacturing, and decided to make at least 50% of Lenovo's manufacturing in-house. Lenovo Chief Technology Officer George He said that vertical integration is having an important role in product development. He stated, "If you look at the industry trends, most innovations for" PCs, smartphones, tablets and smart TVs are related to innovation of key components—display, battery and storage. Differentiation of key parts is so important. So we started investing more ... and working very closely with key parts suppliers."<sup id="cite_ref-WS_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WS-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Previously, lack of integration due to numerous foreign acquisitions and an excessive number of "key performance indicators" (KPIs) was making Lenovo's expansion expensive and creating unacceptably slow delivery times to end-customers. Lenovo responded by reducing the number of KPIs from 150 to 5, offering intensive training to managers, and working to create a global Lenovo culture. Lenovo also doubled-down on vertical integration and manufacturing near target markets in order to cut costs at time when its competitors were making increased use of outsourcing off-shoring. By 2013, Lenovo ranked 20th on Gartner's list of top 50 supply chains, whereas in 2010 the company was unranked.<sup id="cite_ref-Big1_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Big1-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Lenovo partially moved production of its ThinkPad line of computers to Japan. ThinkPads will be produced by NEC in <a href="/wiki/Yamagata_Prefecture" title="Yamagata Prefecture">Yamagata Prefecture</a>. Akemi Watanabe<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">渡辺朱美</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Watanabe Akemi</i></span><span style="margin-left:.09em">)</span></span>, president of Lenovo Japan, said, "As a Japanese, I am glad to see the return to domestic production and the goal is to realize full-scale production as this will improve our image and make the products more acceptable to Japanese customers."<sup id="cite_ref-WS_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WS-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SOFT_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOFT-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2012, Lenovo announced that it would start assembling computers in <a href="/wiki/Whitsett,_North_Carolina" title="Whitsett, North Carolina">Whitsett</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>. Production of desktop and laptop computers, including the <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad_Helix" title="ThinkPad Helix">ThinkPad Helix</a> began in January 2013. As of July 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 115 workers were employed at this facility. Lenovo has been in Whitsett since 2008, where it also has centers for logistics, customer service, and return processing.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Lenovo and Hong Kong <a href="/wiki/Cyberport" title="Cyberport">Cyberport</a> Management Company Limited, a government-sponsored business park for technology firms, reached a deal to "jointly build a cloud service and product research and development center".<sup id="cite_ref-auto_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo's Asia Pacific data center will also be housed in Cyperport.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo assembles smartphones in Chennai, India through a contract manufacturing agreement with <a href="/wiki/Flex_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flex (company)">Flex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Flex_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flex-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In November 2015, Lenovo announced that it would start manufacturing computers in Pondicherry.<sup id="cite_ref-India2_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India2-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accusations_of_slave_labor_by_supplier">Accusations of slave labor by supplier</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Accusations of slave labor by supplier"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In August 2020, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Intercept" title="The Intercept">The Intercept</a></i> reported that Lenovo imported about 258,000 laptops from the Chinese manufacturer Hefei Bitland Information Technology, a company, among others, accused by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Strategic_Policy_Institute" title="Australian Strategic Policy Institute">Australian Strategic Policy Institute</a> of using <a href="/wiki/Uyghurs" title="Uyghurs">Uyghur</a> <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Uyghurs_in_China#Forced_labor" title="Persecution of Uyghurs in China">forced labor</a>. In July 2020, the United States Commerce Department added 11 companies, including Hefei Bitland, implicated in human rights abuses on the <a href="/wiki/Entity_List" title="Entity List">Entity List</a>. Lenovo took some shipments out of the distribution, but other shipments were distributed to consumers.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late July, Lenovo informed its customers it had stopped manufacturing with Bitland and was moving production of related devices to other suppliers.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Response_to_2022_sanctions_against_Russia">Response to 2022 sanctions against Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Response to 2022 sanctions against Russia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="Russian invasion of Ukraine">Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>, Lenovo reportedly suspended shipping to Russia on or before February 25, 2022, and, although it didn't confirm the suspension, faced a domestic backlash from Internet users in China.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Taikoo_Place.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Taikoo_Place.jpg/220px-Taikoo_Place.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Taikoo_Place.jpg/330px-Taikoo_Place.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Taikoo_Place.jpg/440px-Taikoo_Place.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Lenovo's <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Taikoo_Place" title="Taikoo Place">Taikoo Place</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Alongside Beijing, the company has operational centres in <a href="/wiki/Lorong_Chuan" title="Lorong Chuan">Lorong Chuan</a>, Singapore, and <a href="/wiki/Morrisville,_North_Carolina" title="Morrisville, North Carolina">Morrisville, North Carolina</a><sup id="cite_ref-Lenovocontact_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovocontact-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> (near <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Research_Triangle" title="Research Triangle">Research Triangle</a> metropolitan area)<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-McGregor204_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGregor204-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> As of October 2012, the Morrisville facility has about 2,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo identifies its facilities in Beijing, Singapore, and Morrisville as its "key location addresses",<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> where its principal operations occur.<sup id="cite_ref-Lenovocontact_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovocontact-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The company's <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a> is on the 23rd floor of the Lincoln House building of the <a href="/wiki/Taikoo_Place" title="Taikoo Place">Taikoo Place</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quarry_Bay" title="Quarry Bay">Quarry Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Previously the company's U.S. headquarters were in <a href="/wiki/Purchase,_New_York" title="Purchase, New York">Purchase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_York" title="Harrison, New York">Harrison, New York</a>. About 70 people worked there. In 2006, Lenovo announced that it was consolidating its U.S. headquarters, a logistics facility in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a>, and a call center in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, to a new facility in Morrisville. The company received offers of over $11 million in incentive funds from the local Morrisville, North Carolina, area and from the State of North Carolina on the condition that the company employs about 2,200 people.<sup id="cite_ref-Hogan1_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hogan1-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In early 2016, Lenovo carried out a comprehensive restructuring of its business units.<sup id="cite_ref-COMRES_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COMRES-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financials_and_market_share">Financials and market share</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Financials and market share"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the third quarter of 2020, Lenovo commands a leading market share of 25.7 per cent of all PCs sold in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Gartner2_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gartner2-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2013, Lenovo was included as a constituent stock in the <a href="/wiki/Hang_Seng_Index" title="Hang Seng Index">Hang Seng Index</a>. Lenovo replaced the unprofitable <a href="/wiki/Aluminum_Corporation_of_China_Limited" title="Aluminum Corporation of China Limited">Aluminum Corporation of China Limited</a>, a state-owned enterprise, on the list of 50 key companies on the Hong Kong stock exchange that constitute the Hang Seng Index.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The inclusion of Lenovo and Tencent, China's largest internet firm, significantly increased the weight of the technology sector on the index. Being added to the Hang Seng Index was a significant boon for Lenovo and its shareholders as it widened the pool of investors willing to purchase Lenovo's stock. For instance, index funds pegged to the Hang Seng and pension funds that consider index inclusion now have the opportunity to invest in Lenovo.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMP22_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMP22-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013 Lenovo reported that they had achieved double-digit market share in the United States for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Ownership"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/China_Oceanwide_Holdings_Group" title="China Oceanwide Holdings Group">China Oceanwide Holdings Group</a>, a private <a href="/wiki/Investment_company" title="Investment company">Investment company</a> based in Beijing, bought 29% of <a href="/wiki/Legend_Holdings" title="Legend Holdings">Legend Holdings</a>, the parent company of Lenovo, for <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">¥</a>2.76 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> As of 31&#160;March&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 65% of Lenovo stock was held by the general public, 29% by Legend Holdings, 5.8% by Yang Yuanqing, and 0.2% by other directors.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Responding to claims that Lenovo is a <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">state-owned enterprise</a>, CEO Yang Yuanqing said, "Our company is a 100% market oriented company. Some people have said we are a state-owned enterprise. It's 100% not true. In 1984 the Chinese Academy of Sciences only invested $25,000 in our company. The purpose of the Chinese Academy of Sciences to invest in this company was that they wanted to commercialize their research results. The Chinese Academy of Sciences is a pure research entity in China, owned by the government. From this point, you could say we're different from state-owned enterprises. Secondly, after this investment, this company is run totally by the founders and management team. The government has never been involved in our daily operation, in important decisions, strategic direction, nomination of the CEO and top executives and financial management. Everything is done by our management team."<sup id="cite_ref-state_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Chinese Academy of Sciences">Chinese Academy of Sciences</a>, owns 11.7% of Lenovo and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> owns 37.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-giant_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-giant-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2006, the U.S. State Department was harshly criticized for purchasing 16,000 computers from Lenovo. Critics argued that Lenovo was controlled by the Chinese government and a potential vehicle for espionage against the United States. Yang spoke out forcefully and publicly to defend Lenovo. He said, "We are not a government-controlled company." He pointed out that Lenovo pioneered China's transition to a market economy and that in the early 1990s had fought and beaten four state-owned enterprises that dominated the Chinese computer market. Those firms had the full backing of the state while Lenovo received no special treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The State Department deal went through. Yang worried that fears about Lenovo's supposed connections to the Chinese government would be an ongoing issue in the United States. Yang worked to ease worries by communicating directly with Congress.
</p><p>Yang dramatically increased his ownership stake by acquiring 797 million shares in 2011. As of June 2011, Yang owned an 8 per cent stake in Lenovo. He previously owned only 70 million shares. In a statement, Yang said, "While the transaction is a personal financial matter, I want to be very clear that my decision to make this investment is based on my strong belief in the company's very bright future. Our culture is built on commitment and ownership&#160;– we do what we say, and we own what we do. My decision to increase my holdings represents my steadfast belief in these principles."<sup id="cite_ref-ownership_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ownership-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_culture">Corporate culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Corporate culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo's senior executives rotate between the three head offices at Beijing, Singapore, and Morrisville, as well as Lenovo's research and development centre in Yamato, Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-Econ1_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ1-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Leadership"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Yang_Yuanqing">Yang Yuanqing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Yang Yuanqing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yang_Yuanqing" title="Yang Yuanqing">Yang Yuanqing</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Yang_Yuanqing.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Yang_Yuanqing.jpeg/220px-Yang_Yuanqing.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/61/Yang_Yuanqing.jpeg 1.5x" data-file-width="321" data-file-height="317" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Yang_Yuanqing" title="Yang Yuanqing">Yang Yuanqing</a>, Lenovo's Chairman and CEO</figcaption></figure>
<p>Yang Yuanqing is the chairman and chief executive officer of Lenovo. One of his major achievements was leading Lenovo to become the best-selling personal computer brand in China since 1997. In 2001, <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">Bloomberg Businessweek</a></i> named him one of Asia's rising stars in business.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Yang was president and CEO of Lenovo until 2004, when Lenovo closed its acquisition of IBM's PC division, after which Yang was succeeded as Lenovo CEO by IBM's <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ward_(businessman)" title="Steve Ward (businessman)">Stephen M. Ward Jr.</a> Ward was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/William_Amelio" title="William Amelio">William Amelio</a> on 20 December 2005. In February 2009, Yang replaced Amelio as CEO and has served in that capacity ever since. Yang was chairman of Lenovo's board from 2004 to 2008, and returned as chairman in 2012 alongside his role as CEO.
</p><p>In 2012, Yang received a $3 million bonus as a reward for record profits, which he in turn redistributed to about 10,000 of Lenovo's employees. According to Lenovo spokesman, Jeffrey Shafer, Yang felt that it would be the right thing to, "redirect [the money] to the employees as a real tangible gesture for what they done." Shafer also said that Yang, who owns about eight per cent of Lenovo's stock, "felt that he was rewarded well simply as the owner of the company".<sup id="cite_ref-Bonus_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonus-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> The bonuses were mostly distributed among staff working in positions such as production and reception who received an average of CN¥2,000 or about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$314</span>. This was almost equivalent to a monthly salary of an average worker in China.<sup id="cite_ref-WPBlog_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPBlog-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Yang made a similar gift of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3.25 million</span> again in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Huff_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huff-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Lenovo's annual report, Yang earned <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$14 million</span>, including <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$5.2 million</span> in bonuses, during the fiscal year that ended in March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-CNNBonus_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNNBonus-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, <i>Barron's</i> named Yang one of the "World's Best CEOs".<sup id="cite_ref-Best_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Liu_Chuanzhi">Liu Chuanzhi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Liu Chuanzhi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Liu_Chuanzhi" title="Liu Chuanzhi">Liu Chuanzhi</a></div>
<p>Liu Chuanzhi is the founder and former chairman of Lenovo. Liu was trained as an engineer at a military college and later went on to work at the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Chinese Academy of Sciences">Chinese Academy of Sciences</a>. Like many young people during the Cultural Revolution, Liu was denounced and sent to the countryside where he worked as a laborer on a rice farm. Liu claims <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a> as a key source of inspiration. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> he stated that "Our earliest and best teacher was Hewlett-Packard." For more than ten years, Lenovo was Hewlett-Packard's distributor in China.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> In reference to Lenovo's later acquisition of IBM's personal computer unit Liu said, "I remember the first time I took part in a meeting of IBM agents. I was wearing an old business suit of my father's and I sat in the back row. Even in my dreams, I never imagined that one day we could buy the IBM PC business. It was unthinkable. Impossible."<sup id="cite_ref-chief_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chief-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Board of directors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early 2013, Lenovo announced the addition of <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang" title="Jerry Yang">Jerry Yang</a> to its board.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJJerryYang_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJJerryYang-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo's CEO Yang Yuanqing said, "Jerry's appointment as an observer to our board furthers Lenovo's reputation as a transparent international company." Just prior to the appointment of Jerry Yang, Tudor Brown, the founder of British semiconductor design firm <a href="/wiki/Arm_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arm (company)">ARM</a>, was also appointed to Lenovo's board. Speaking of both men Yang Yuanqing said, "We believe that they will add a great deal to our strategic thinking, long-term direction and, ultimately, our ability to achieve our aspirations in the PC plus era."
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_and_sponsorships">Marketing and sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Marketing and sponsorships"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2009, Lenovo became the first personal computer manufacturer to divide countries into emerging markets and mature markets. Lenovo then developed a different set of strategies for each category. Lenovo's competitors have widely adopted the same approach<sup id="cite_ref-People_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-People-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Lenovo made a major effort to expand its market share in developing economies such as Brazil and India through acquisitions and increased budgets for marketing and advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-Econ1_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ1-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celebrity_sponsorships_and_endorsements">Celebrity sponsorships and endorsements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Celebrity sponsorships and endorsements"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2013, Lenovo announced that it had hired American actor <a href="/wiki/Ashton_Kutcher" title="Ashton Kutcher">Ashton Kutcher</a> as a product engineer and spokesman. David Roman, Lenovo's chief marketing officer, said, "His partnership goes beyond traditional bounds by deeply integrating him into our organization as a product engineer. Ashton will help us break new ground by challenging assumptions, bringing a new perspective and contributing his technical expertise to Yoga Tablet and other devices."<sup id="cite_ref-Ash_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ash-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kobe_Bryant" title="Kobe Bryant">Kobe Bryant</a> became an official ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_smartphones" title="Lenovo smartphones">Lenovo smartphones</a> in China and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> in early 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Bryant appeared in a social campaign titled "The Everyday Kobe Challenge" for the launch of <a href="/wiki/Lenovo_IdeaPhone_K900" title="Lenovo IdeaPhone K900">Lenovo IdeaPhone K900</a> in Malaysia, Thailand, Indonesia and the Philippines in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT2_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_sponsorship">Sporting sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sporting sponsorship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg/170px-Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg/255px-Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg/340px-Official_2008_Summer_Olympics_Torch_in_Vilnius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> Torch was designed by Lenovo.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Lenovo was an official computer sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>. When asked about Lenovo's brand Yang Yuanqing said, "The Beijing Olympics were very good for brand awareness in countries like the US and Argentina, but not good enough."<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The NFL has been a Lenovo customer since 2007. In July 2012, Lenovo and the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) announced that Lenovo had become the NFL's "Official Laptop, Desktop and Workstation Sponsor." Lenovo said that this was its largest sponsorship deal ever in the United States. NFL stars <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rice" title="Jerry Rice">Jerry Rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/DeAngelo_Williams" title="DeAngelo Williams">DeAngelo Williams</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Torry_Holt" title="Torry Holt">Torry Holt</a> were on hand for the announcement and a celebration with 1,500 Lenovo employees. Lenovo's sponsorship will last at least three years.<sup id="cite_ref-NFL_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFL-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo also become technology partner for <a href="/wiki/Ducati_Corse" title="Ducati Corse">Ducati Corse</a> in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_motorcycle_racing" title="Grand Prix motorcycle racing">Grand Prix motorcycle racing</a> since 2018. And for the <a href="/wiki/2021_MotoGP_World_Championship" title="2021 MotoGP World Championship">2021 MotoGP</a> it will become main sponsor for the Bolognese.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo is also an official partner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL's</a> <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Hurricanes" title="Carolina Hurricanes">Carolina Hurricanes</a> who play in nearby <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_North_Carolina" title="Raleigh, North Carolina">Raleigh, North Carolina</a>.
</p><p>Lenovo and <a href="/wiki/FC_Internazionale" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Internazionale">FC Internazionale</a>, in 2019, have signed a multi-year sponsorship agreement that makes Lenovo the Global Technology Partner of the Nerazzurri company.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> In May 2021, Lenovo and <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola Mobility</a> decided to celebrate with a limited edition of <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Razr_(2020)" title="Motorola Razr (2020)">Motorola Razr</a> totally customized and produced in 2021 numbered pieces, to honor Inter who won their 19th <a href="/wiki/Scudetto" title="Scudetto">Scudetto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> In July 2021 there was the launch of the new Inter Home shirt for the <a href="/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_Inter_Milan_season" title="2021–22 Inter Milan season">2021–22 season</a>, they unveiled the introduction of Lenovo as a sponsor on the back of the shirt.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Television.2C_internet.2C_and_other_media"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Television,_internet,_and_other_media">Television, internet, and other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television, internet, and other media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo used a short-film entitled <i>The Pursuit</i> in its "For Those Who Do" campaign launched in 2011. The film depicted a mysterious young woman using the IdeaPad Yoga 13 to stay one-step-ahead of her evil pursuers. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Campbell" title="Martin Campbell">Martin Campbell</a>, who previously worked on action movies and James Bond films such as GoldenEye and the remake of Casino Royale, shot this film. Lenovo was the first Chinese company to make use of such marketing techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-Big1_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Big1-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2015, Lenovo hosted its first ever "Tech World" conference in Beijing.<sup id="cite_ref-TW1_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TW1-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ZUK_Mobile" title="ZUK Mobile">ZUK Mobile</a>, a separate company formed by Lenovo in 2014, announced several products at Tech World, These included slim power banks, 3D printers that can print food such as chocolate, an outdoor sound box, and a Wi-Fi based control system for <a href="/wiki/Home_automation" title="Home automation">home automation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TW1_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TW1-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: China"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In its home market China, Lenovo has a vast distribution network designed to make sure that there is at least one shop selling Lenovo computers within 50 kilometers of nearly all consumers. Lenovo has also developed close relationships with its Chinese distributors, who are granted exclusive territories and only carry Lenovo products.<sup id="cite_ref-Econ1_81-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Econ1-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of July 2013, Lenovo believes that urbanization initiatives being pushed by former Premier <a href="/wiki/Li_Keqiang" title="Li Keqiang">Li Keqiang</a> will allow it to sustain sales growth in China for the foreseeable future. Speaking at Lenovo's annual general meeting in Hong Kong in 2013, Yang Yuanqing said: "I believe urbanisation will help us further increase the overall [domestic] PC market." Yang also stressed the opportunity presented by the China's relatively low penetration rate of personal computers. Lenovo previously benefited from the Chinese government's rural subsidies, part of a wider economic stimulus initiative, designed to increase purchases of appliances and electronics. That program, which Lenovo joined in 2004, ended in 2011. Lenovo enjoys consistent price premiums over its traditional competitors in rural markets and a stronger local sales and service presence.<sup id="cite_ref-FT2_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT2-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: India"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo has gained significant market share in India through bulk orders to large companies and government agencies. For example, the government of <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a> ordered a million <a href="/wiki/ThinkPad" title="ThinkPad">ThinkPads</a> from IBM/Lenovo in 2012 and single-handedly made the firm a market leader. Lenovo distributes most of the personal computers it sells in India through five national distributors such as <a href="/wiki/Ingram_Micro" title="Ingram Micro">Ingram Micro</a> and Redington.<sup id="cite_ref-India6_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India6-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Given that most smartphones and tablets are sold to individuals Lenovo is pursuing a different strategy making use of many small state-centric distributors. Amar Babu, Lenovo's managing director for India, said, "To reach out to small towns and the hinterland, we have tied up with 40 regional distributors. We want our distributors to be exclusive to us. We will, in turn, ensure they have exclusive rights to distribute Lenovo products in their catchment area."<sup id="cite_ref-India6_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India6-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> As of 2013, Lenovo had about 6,000 retailers selling smartphones and tablets in India. In February 2013, Lenovo established a relationship with Reliance Communications to sell smartphones. The smartphones carried by Reliance have dual-SIM capability and support both GSM and CDMA. Babu claims that the relative under penetration of smartphones in India represents an opportunity for Lenovo.<sup id="cite_ref-India6_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India6-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo has assembled a team of senior managers familiar with the Indian market, launched mobile phones at all price points there, and worked on branding to build market share. As of February 2014, Lenovo claims that its sales of smartphones in India have been increasing 100% per quarter while the market is only growing 15–20% over the same period. Lenovo did marketing tests of its smartphones in November 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> and some southern cities, where Lenovo already had a strong presence. Lenovo's strategy has been to create awareness, maintain a broad selection of phones at all price points, and develop distribution networks. Lenovo partnered with two national distributors and over 100 local distributors. As of February 2014, more than 7,000 retail outlets in India sold Lenovo smartphones. Lenovo has also partnered with HCL in order to set up 250 service centres in 110 cities.<sup id="cite_ref-India1_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India1-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In India, Lenovo grants distributors exclusive territories but allows them to sell computers from other companies. Lenovo uses its close relationships with distributors to gain <a href="/wiki/Market_intelligence" title="Market intelligence">market intelligence</a> and speed up product development.
</p><p>Lenovo reported a year-on-year increase of about 951% in tablet sales in India for the first quarter of 2014. Canalys, a market research firm, said Lenovo took market share away from Apple and Samsung in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-IndiaGrowth_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiaGrowth-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Africa"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo first started doing business in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, establishing a sales office, and then expanded to East African markets such as Kenya, Tanzania, Ethiopia, Uganda, and Rwanda. West Africa followed when Lenovo set-up a Nigerian legal office and then expanded to Ghana, Zimbabwe, Mozambique and Botswana.
</p><p>According to Lenovo's general manager for Africa, Graham Braum, Lenovo's strategy is to put "great emphasis on products that sell well in Africa" and roll out "products alongside different African governments' rolling out of wireless technology". Products such as the Lenovo Yoga series are popular in Africa because of their long battery life, as many areas have unreliable electrical supply. Other popular products include the Lenovo netbooks, which were introduced in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-dexing_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dexing-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lenovo picked Nigeria in 2013 to release its smartphone because unlike South Africa and other African countries, there is no requirement to partner with a local telecom firm to sell its phones.<sup id="cite_ref-Africa1_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Africa1-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the long term, according to Braum, "Lenovo in Africa will focus on continuing to consistently supply personal computer products and allow this market to grow, while moving into new territory such as mobile and enterprise."<sup id="cite_ref-dexing_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dexing-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Singapore"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo has had a presence in Singapore as early as its foundation, and with a focus on the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> region, it is the location of one of Lenovo's three head offices.<sup id="cite_ref-LNSG_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LNSG-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Registered as Lenovo<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> (Singapore) Pte. Ltd., it is located at the New Tech Park in the <a href="/wiki/Lorong_Chuan" title="Lorong Chuan">Lorong Chuan</a> district of the <a href="/wiki/North-East_Region,_Singapore" title="North-East Region, Singapore">North-East Region</a> of Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-LNSG_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LNSG-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: United States"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the United States, Lenovo began the "For Those Who Do" marketing campaign in 2010, created by the ad agency <a href="/wiki/Saatchi_%26_Saatchi" title="Saatchi &amp; Saatchi">Saatchi &amp; Saatchi</a>. It was part of Lenovo's first-ever global branding campaign, beyond its domestic market in China.<sup id="cite_ref-fc_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fc-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> "For Those Who Do" was designed to appeal to young consumers in the 18- to 25-year-old demographic by stressing its utility to creative individuals that Lenovo's advertising refers to as "doers".<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> One of Lenovo's operational centers is located in North Carolina, United States. Lenovo also started manufacturing products in the United States in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goodweird">Goodweird</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Goodweird"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lenovo launched a multi-year advertising campaign called "Goodweird" in the last half of 2015. Goodweird is designed to convey the idea that designs that seem strange initially often become familiar and widely accepted. The Goodweird campaign includes a video with famous images of early attempts to fly with the aid of homemade wings and a bicycle that transitions to a modern-day shot of a man soaring across mountains in a wingsuit before transitioning again to a shot of the <a href="/wiki/Stealth_Bomber" class="mw-redirect" title="Stealth Bomber">Stealth Bomber</a>. Lenovo worked with three agencies on Goodweird: London-based DLKW Low, We Are Social, and Blast Radius. Goodweird is part of Lenovo's wider strategy to appeal to millennials with an emphasis on design trendsetters. A portion of the funding for Goodweird is being directed to prominent <a href="/wiki/List_of_YouTubers" title="List of YouTubers">YouTubers</a> and Viners. <a href="/wiki/BuzzFeed" title="BuzzFeed">BuzzFeed</a> has been engaged to create relevant content.<sup id="cite_ref-Goodweird_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goodweird-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_and_privacy_incidents">Security and privacy incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Security and privacy incidents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Superfish">Superfish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Superfish"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2015, Lenovo became the subject of controversy for having bundled software identified as <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a> on some of its laptops. The software, <a href="/wiki/Superfish" title="Superfish">Superfish</a> Visual Discovery, is a web browser add-on that injects <a href="/wiki/Pricing" title="Pricing">Pricing</a> advertising into search engine results pages. To <a href="/wiki/Man-in-the-middle_attack" title="Man-in-the-middle attack">intercept</a> <a href="/wiki/HTTPS" title="HTTPS">HTTPS</a>-encrypted communications, the software also installed a self-signed <a href="/wiki/Public_key_certificate" title="Public key certificate">public key certificate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-zdnet-superfish_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zdnet-superfish-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-verge-superfish_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-verge-superfish-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> When the Superfish <a href="/wiki/Public-key_cryptography" title="Public-key cryptography">public-key cryptography</a> was compromised, it was also discovered that the same private key was used across all installations of the software, leaving users vulnerable to security exploits utilizing the key.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-superfish_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-superfish-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lenovo&#39;s_Superfish_&#39;Malware&#39;_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lenovo&#39;s_Superfish_&#39;Malware&#39;-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo made between <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7005200000000000000♠"></span><span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>200,000 to 250,000</span> on its deal with Superfish.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 Lenovo agreed to pay <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3.5 million</span> as part of a settlement with the US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> and announced an apology to its customers and stock holders.
</p><p>The head of Superfish responded to security concerns by saying the vulnerability was "inadvertently" introduced by Komodia, which built the application.<sup id="cite_ref-fallout_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fallout-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> In response to the criticism, Lenovo detailed that it would cease further distribution and use of the Superfish software, and offered affected customers free six-month subscriptions to the <a href="/wiki/McAfee" title="McAfee">McAfee</a> LiveSafe software.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo issued a promise to reduce the amount of "<a href="/wiki/Software_bloat" title="Software bloat">Software bloat</a>" it bundles with its <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a> devices, promising to only include Lenovo software, security software, drivers, and "certain applications customarily expected by users".<sup id="cite_ref-maxpc-nomorebloat_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maxpc-nomorebloat-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Salon.com" title="Salon.com">Salon</a></i> tech writer David Auerbach compared the Superfish incident to the <a href="/wiki/Sony_BMG_copy_protection_rootkit_scandal" title="Sony BMG copy protection rootkit scandal">Sony DRM rootkit scandal</a>, and argued that "installing Superfish is one of the most irresponsible mistakes an established tech company has ever made."<sup id="cite_ref-salon_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lenovo_Service_Engine">Lenovo Service Engine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Lenovo Service Engine"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From October 2014 through June 2015, the <a href="/wiki/UEFI" title="UEFI">UEFI</a> firmware on certain Lenovo models had contained software known as "Lenovo Service Engine", which Lenovo says automatically sent non-identifiable system information to Lenovo the first time Windows is connected to the internet, and on laptops, automatically installs the Lenovo OneKey Optimizer program (software considered to be <a href="/wiki/Software_bloat" title="Software bloat">Software bloat</a>) as well. This process occurs even on clean installations of Windows. It was found that this program had been automatically installed using a new feature in <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Features_new_to_Windows_8#Windows_Platform_Binary_Table" title="Features new to Windows 8">Windows Platform Binary Table</a>, which allows executable files to be stored within UEFI firmware for execution on startup, and is meant to "allow critical software to persist even when the operating system has changed or been reinstalled in a "clean" configuration"; specifically, anti-theft security software. The software was discontinued after it was found that aspects of the software had security vulnerabilities, and did not comply with revised guidelines for appropriate usage of WPBT. On 31 July 2015, Lenovo released instructions and UEFI firmware updates meant to remove Lenovo Service Engine.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-windowsantitheft_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-windowsantitheft-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-techrepublic-wpbt_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techrepublic-wpbt-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pcw-lenovoservice_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcw-lenovoservice-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lenovo_Customer_Feedback_program">Lenovo Customer Feedback program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Lenovo Customer Feedback program"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At a third time in 2015, criticism arose that Lenovo might have installed software that looked suspicious on their commercial Think-PC lines. This was discovered by Computerworld writer Michael Horowitz, who had purchased several Think systems with the Customer Feedback program installed, which seemed to log usage data and metrics.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Further analysis by Horowitz revealed however that this was mostly harmless, as it was only logging the usage of some pre-installed Lenovo programs, and not the usage in general, and only if the user allowed the data to be collected. Horowitz also criticized other media for quoting his original article and saying that Lenovo preinstalled spyware, as he himself never used that term in this case and he also said that he does not consider the software he found to be spyware.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lenovo_Accelerator">Lenovo Accelerator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Lenovo Accelerator"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of June 2016, a Duo Labs report stated that Lenovo was still installing bloatware, some of which leads to security vulnerabilities as soon as the user turns on their new PC.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Lenovo advised users to remove the offending app, "Lenovo Accelerator".<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> According to Lenovo, the app, designed to "speed up the loading" of Lenovo applications, created a <a href="/wiki/Man-in-the-middle" class="mw-redirect" title="Man-in-the-middle">man-in-the-middle</a> security vulnerability.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Marine_network_security_breach">U.S. Marine network security breach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lenovo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: U.S. Marine network security breach"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2021, <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">Bloomberg Businessweek</a></i> reported that U.S. investigators found in 2008 that military units in Iraq were using Lenovo laptops in which the hardware had been altered. According to a testimony from the case in 2010, "A large amount of Lenovo laptops were sold to the U.S. military that had a chip encrypted on the motherboard that would record all the data that was being inputted into that laptop and send it back to China". Lenovo was unaware of the testimony and the U.S. military did not inform the company of any security concerns. A Lenovo spokesperson stated that "we have no way to assess the allegations you cite or whether security concerns may have been triggered by third-party interference."<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-LNSG-211"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-LNSG_211-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-LNSG_211-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1215172403"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.lenovo.com/sg/en/lenovo/locations/">"Locations | Lenovo Singapore"</a>. <i>www.lenovo.com</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">16 February</span> 2022</span>. <q>Address: 151 Lorong Chuan #02-01 New Tech Park Singapore 556741</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=www.lenovo.com&amp;rft.atitle=Locations+%7C+Lenovo+Singapore&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.lenovo.com%2Fsg%2Fen%2Flenovo%2Flocations%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALenovo" class="Z3988"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-212"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-212">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the past, Lenovo has maintained a strong presence in Singapore since its foundation. Over the years, its focus on the Southeast Asia region has led to the establishment of one of Lenovo's three head offices in Singapore. Previously known as Lenovo (Singapore) Pte. Ltd., the company operated from the New Tech Park in the Lorong Chuan district, situated in the North-East Region of Singapore.

However, in the present, Lenovo continues to thrive and evolve in Singapore. The company remains committed to the Southeast Asia market and has expanded its operations and engagement in the region. The office, still registered as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.lenovo.com/sg/en">Lenovo</a> (Singapore) Pte. Ltd., remains strategically located at the New Tech Park in the Lorong Chuan district. This location provides numerous advantages, such as access to key markets and a flourishing business environment in Singapore, which supports Lenovo's growth and success in the region.

Throughout the years, Lenovo's presence in Singapore has transitioned from its early establishment to a dynamic and forward-looking operation. The company's commitment to the Southeast Asia market and its continued investment in Singapore reflect its recognition of the region's strategic importance and the opportunities it presents.</span>
</li>
